Salaf and Khalaf: Two Valid Approaches to Divine Attributes
Comparison of Salaf and Khalaf methods with endorsement of both.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why both the Salaf and Khalaf methodologies for interpreting divine attributes are legitimate and ultimately lead to the same conclusion: Allah's transcendence.

Core Idea
Two paths, one goal: both Salaf and Khalaf affirm that Allah is unlike any creation.

This passage from al-Būṭī clarifies a common misconception: the difference between the early and later scholars is not a contradiction in doctrine. Rather, each method was appropriate for its time. As you read, notice how the author defends both while warning against those who distort the texts.

Guided Path
1
Read the Passage
Read the Arabic and translation. Pay attention to how the author describes both methodologies.
The passage includes a famous quote from Imam Malik about al-istiwāʾ.
2
Identify the Salaf Method
Understand Imam Malik's response: accepting the word without asking 'how'.
This is the method of tafwīḍ (consigning knowledge to Allah).
3
Understand the Khalaf Method
See why the later scholars had to use rhetorical analysis due to intellectual challenges and heretics.
Both methods lead to affirming Allah's transcendence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واعلم أن مذهب السلف في عصرهم كان هو الأفضل والأسلم ، والأوفق مع الإيمان الفطري المرتكز في كل من العقل والقلب . ومذهب الخلف في عصرهم أصبح هو المصير الذي لا يمكن التحول عنه ، بسبب ما قامت فيه من المذاهب الفكرية والمناقشات العلمية ، وبسبب ظهور البلاغة العربية مقعدة في قواعد من المجاز والتشبيه والاستعارة . یکن بوسع وهكذا ، فقد كان بوسع الإمام مالك رحمه الله أن يقول في عصره لـذلـك الذي سأله عن معنى الاستواء في الآية : الكيف غير معقول ، والاستواء غير مجهول ، والإيمان به واجب ، والسؤال عنه بدعة . إذ كان العصر عصر إيمان ويقين راسخين، بسبب قرب العهد بعصر النبوة وامتداد الإشراق إليه . ولكن لم الأئمة الذين قاموا في عصر التدوين وازدهار العلوم واتساع حلقات البحث وفنون البلاغة أن يسلّموا ذلك التسليم دون أن يحللوا هذه النصوص على ضوء ما انتهوا إليه من فنون البلاغة والمجاز ، خصوصاً وإن فيهم الزنادقة الذين لا يقنعهم منهج التسليم ، ويتظاهرون بالحاجة إلى الفهم التفصيلي ، وإن كانوا في حقيقة الأمر معاندين والمهم أن تعلم بأن كلاً من المذهبين منهجان إلى غاية واحدة ، لأن المآل فيها إلى أن الله عز وجل لا يشبهه شيء من مخلـوقـاتـه وأنـه منزه عن جميـع النقص . فالخلاف الذي تراه بينهما خلاف لفظي وشكلي فقط صفات هذا ، وليس لنا شأن في هذا المقام ، بتلك الطوائف التي شذت ، ممن يقال عنهم المعطلة ، أو المجسمة ، وهم الذين تخيلوا الله عز وجل في صورة جسم ، ثم ذهبوا يتخيلون له الشكل والسمت الذي يريدون ، متمسكين بظواهر هذه النصوص ومعرضين عن النصوص القاطعة الأخرى ، ومتجاهلين طبيعة هذه اللغة وما فيها من مجاز واستعارة وأساليب مختلفة في التعبير . فهؤلاء لا يقام لهم أي حساب فيما يتعلق بكتاب الله تعالى وتفسيره وليسوا من نصوصه - محكمه أو متشابهه - في شيء . وإنما هم قوم تصوروا الذات الإلهية كما صورته أخيلتهم المجردة ، ثم استنهضوا آيات من كتاب الله تعالى إلى تلك الأخيلة لتصدقها وتؤمن لهم بها ، وأنى لآيات الله الباهرة أن تدلّ إلا على الحق المنير ، فعادوا يعكفون على أصنام لهم أقاموها في رؤوسهم بدلاً من أن ينصبوها أمام أعينهم . وليس أصدق في وصف حالهم مما قال الله عز وجل عنهم : ﴿ فَأَمَّا الَّذِينَ فِي قُلُوبِهِمْ زَيْغٌ فَيَتَّبِعونَ ما تَشابَة مِنْهُ ابْتِغَاءَ الفِتْنَةِ وابتغاء تأويله ) و آل عمران : ٧]
And know that the way of the Salaf in their era was the best and safest, and most consonant with the innate faith rooted in both reason and the heart. And the way of the Khalaf in their era became the unavoidable course, due to the intellectual trends and scientific discussions that arose, and due to the emergence of Arabic eloquence established in the rules of metaphor (al-majāz), similitude (al-tashbīh), and allegory (al-istiʿārah). (unclear fragment) And thus, Imam Malik, may God have mercy on him, was able to say in his time to the one who asked him about the meaning of al-istiwāʾ in the verse: 'The modality (al-kayf) is not comprehensible, and al-istiwāʾ is not unknown, and belief in it is obligatory, and asking about it is an innovation.' For that era was an era of firm faith and certainty, due to the proximity to the era of prophethood and the extension of its illumination. But the imams who arose in the era of codification and flourishing of sciences and expansion of research circles and arts of eloquence could not accept that acceptance without analyzing these texts in light of what they had attained of the arts of eloquence and metaphor, especially since among them were heretics (zanādiqah) who were not satisfied with the method of submission, and pretended to need detailed understanding, though in reality they were obstinate. And the important thing is that you know that each of the two ways are two paths to one goal, because the final outcome in them is that God Almighty is not similar to any of His creations and that He is transcendent above all deficiency. So the disagreement you see between them is only a verbal and formal disagreement. Attributes. This, and we have no concern in this place with those deviant groups who are called the Muʿaṭṭilah (those who strip God of attributes) or the Mujassimah (anthropomorphists), who imagined God Almighty in the form of a body, then went on to imagine for Him the shape and appearance they desired, clinging to the literal meanings of these texts and turning away from other definitive texts, and ignoring the nature of this language and what it contains of metaphor, allegory, and various modes of expression. So these are of no account whatsoever concerning the Book of God and its interpretation, and they are not [connected] to its texts—its clear or ambiguous—in anything. Rather, they are a people who conceived the Divine Essence as their bare imaginations depicted it, then they recruited verses from the Book of God to support those imaginations so that they would confirm them and guarantee them, but how can God's dazzling verses indicate anything but the clear truth? So they returned to worshipping idols they had erected in their heads instead of erecting them before their eyes. And nothing is truer in describing their condition than what God said about them: 'As for those in whose hearts is deviation, they follow what is ambiguous of it, seeking discord and seeking its interpretation' (Āl ʿImrān 3:7).
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
This passage is a comparative analysis of the methodologies of the Salaf (early Muslims) and the Khalaf (later scholars) regarding the interpretation of divine attributes, followed by a strong condemnation of anthropomorphists. The author begins by stating that the Salaf's method was best for their time because it was most consonant with innate faith. The Khalaf's method became necessary due to intellectual challenges and the development of Arabic rhetorical sciences (balāghah) including metaphor (majāz), similitude (tashbīh), and allegory (istiʿārah). He provides the example of Imam Malik's response about al-istiwāʾ: accepting the term without asking 'how.' The Khalaf, however, had to analyze texts rhetorically because of heretics who demanded detailed explanations. Crucially, the author asserts that both methods lead to the same goal: affirming that God is unlike any creation and transcendent. Thus the difference is merely formal. Then he dismisses the deviant groups: the Muʿaṭṭilah (those who negate attributes) and the Mujassimah (anthropomorphists) who take literal meanings and ignore metaphorical language. He describes them as people who create mental idols and then force verses to support them, quoting Quran 3:7 as a description of their deviation.

Key Terms
مذهب السلف
مذهب الخلف
الاستواء
المجاز
التشبيه
الاستعارة
الزنادقة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Salaf and Khalaf have contradictory doctrines about Allah's attributes.
Correction: Both affirm transcendence; their difference is methodological and verbal.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what is the ultimate goal of both the Salaf and Khalaf methodologies?
A) To negate all attributes
B) To affirm God's transcendence
C) To establish anthropomorphism
D) To create a new method

Key Takeaway
Both Salaf and Khalaf methods affirm Allah's transcendence; their differences are only verbal and situational.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
Imam Malik warned that asking 'how' about divine attributes is an innovation. Is there an area of your faith where you demand clarity from Allah that He hasn't given? How can you practice submission in that area starting today?
?
The Khalaf method arose partly because of heretics who pretended to need detailed understanding. Have you ever used intellectual questions as a shield for doubt or disobedience? What would it take for you to honestly place your intellect under revelation?

Warning Against Anthropomorphism and Distortion of Texts
Condemnation of Muʿaṭṭilah and Mujassimah and explanation of their error.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the error of those who interpret divine attributes literally to imply a body, and why they are excluded from proper interpretation of the Quran.

Core Idea
Those who imagine God as a body are worshipping mental idols, not the true God.

After establishing the legitimacy of both Salaf and Khalaf methods, the author turns to condemn two deviant groups: the Muʿaṭṭilah and the Mujassimah. The latter, especially, are severely criticized for imposing their imaginations on the Quran. This lesson will help you recognize the boundaries of valid interpretation.

Guided Path
1
Read the Condemnation
Read the passage and translation. Notice the author's strong language against the deviant groups.
Pay attention to the Quranic verse at the end.
2
Identify the Two Groups
Understand who the Muʿaṭṭilah (those who strip attributes) and the Mujassimah (anthropomorphists) are.
The author focuses more on the Mujassimah.
3
Understand Their Error
See why they are described as people who create mental idols and force verses to support them.
Their method ignores the metaphorical nature of the Quran.

واعلم أن مذهب السلف في عصرهم كان هو الأفضل والأسلم ، والأوفق مع الإيمان الفطري المرتكز في كل من العقل والقلب . ومذهب الخلف في عصرهم أصبح هو المصير الذي لا يمكن التحول عنه ، بسبب ما قامت فيه من المذاهب الفكرية والمناقشات العلمية ، وبسبب ظهور البلاغة العربية مقعدة في قواعد من المجاز والتشبيه والاستعارة . یکن بوسع وهكذا ، فقد كان بوسع الإمام مالك رحمه الله أن يقول في عصره لـذلـك الذي سأله عن معنى الاستواء في الآية : الكيف غير معقول ، والاستواء غير مجهول ، والإيمان به واجب ، والسؤال عنه بدعة . إذ كان العصر عصر إيمان ويقين راسخين، بسبب قرب العهد بعصر النبوة وامتداد الإشراق إليه . ولكن لم الأئمة الذين قاموا في عصر التدوين وازدهار العلوم واتساع حلقات البحث وفنون البلاغة أن يسلّموا ذلك التسليم دون أن يحللوا هذه النصوص على ضوء ما انتهوا إليه من فنون البلاغة والمجاز ، خصوصاً وإن فيهم الزنادقة الذين لا يقنعهم منهج التسليم ، ويتظاهرون بالحاجة إلى الفهم التفصيلي ، وإن كانوا في حقيقة الأمر معاندين والمهم أن تعلم بأن كلاً من المذهبين منهجان إلى غاية واحدة ، لأن المآل فيها إلى أن الله عز وجل لا يشبهه شيء من مخلـوقـاتـه وأنـه منزه عن جميـع النقص . فالخلاف الذي تراه بينهما خلاف لفظي وشكلي فقط صفات هذا ، وليس لنا شأن في هذا المقام ، بتلك الطوائف التي شذت ، ممن يقال عنهم المعطلة ، أو المجسمة ، وهم الذين تخيلوا الله عز وجل في صورة جسم ، ثم ذهبوا يتخيلون له الشكل والسمت الذي يريدون ، متمسكين بظواهر هذه النصوص ومعرضين عن النصوص القاطعة الأخرى ، ومتجاهلين طبيعة هذه اللغة وما فيها من مجاز واستعارة وأساليب مختلفة في التعبير . فهؤلاء لا يقام لهم أي حساب فيما يتعلق بكتاب الله تعالى وتفسيره وليسوا من نصوصه - محكمه أو متشابهه - في شيء . وإنما هم قوم تصوروا الذات الإلهية كما صورته أخيلتهم المجردة ، ثم استنهضوا آيات من كتاب الله تعالى إلى تلك الأخيلة لتصدقها وتؤمن لهم بها ، وأنى لآيات الله الباهرة أن تدلّ إلا على الحق المنير ، فعادوا يعكفون على أصنام لهم أقاموها في رؤوسهم بدلاً من أن ينصبوها أمام أعينهم . وليس أصدق في وصف حالهم مما قال الله عز وجل عنهم : ﴿ فَأَمَّا الَّذِينَ فِي قُلُوبِهِمْ زَيْغٌ فَيَتَّبِعونَ ما تَشابَة مِنْهُ ابْتِغَاءَ الفِتْنَةِ وابتغاء تأويله ) و آل عمران : ٧]
And know that the way of the Salaf in their era was the best and safest, and most consonant with the innate faith rooted in both reason and the heart. And the way of the Khalaf in their era became the unavoidable course, due to the intellectual trends and scientific discussions that arose, and due to the emergence of Arabic eloquence established in the rules of metaphor (al-majāz), similitude (al-tashbīh), and allegory (al-istiʿārah). (unclear fragment) And thus, Imam Malik, may God have mercy on him, was able to say in his time to the one who asked him about the meaning of al-istiwāʾ in the verse: 'The modality (al-kayf) is not comprehensible, and al-istiwāʾ is not unknown, and belief in it is obligatory, and asking about it is an innovation.' For that era was an era of firm faith and certainty, due to the proximity to the era of prophethood and the extension of its illumination. But the imams who arose in the era of codification and flourishing of sciences and expansion of research circles and arts of eloquence could not accept that acceptance without analyzing these texts in light of what they had attained of the arts of eloquence and metaphor, especially since among them were heretics (zanādiqah) who were not satisfied with the method of submission, and pretended to need detailed understanding, though in reality they were obstinate. And the important thing is that you know that each of the two ways are two paths to one goal, because the final outcome in them is that God Almighty is not similar to any of His creations and that He is transcendent above all deficiency. So the disagreement you see between them is only a verbal and formal disagreement. Attributes. This, and we have no concern in this place with those deviant groups who are called the Muʿaṭṭilah (those who strip God of attributes) or the Mujassimah (anthropomorphists), who imagined God Almighty in the form of a body, then went on to imagine for Him the shape and appearance they desired, clinging to the literal meanings of these texts and turning away from other definitive texts, and ignoring the nature of this language and what it contains of metaphor, allegory, and various modes of expression. So these are of no account whatsoever concerning the Book of God and its interpretation, and they are not [connected] to its texts—its clear or ambiguous—in anything. Rather, they are a people who conceived the Divine Essence as their bare imaginations depicted it, then they recruited verses from the Book of God to support those imaginations so that they would confirm them and guarantee them, but how can God's dazzling verses indicate anything but the clear truth? So they returned to worshipping idols they had erected in their heads instead of erecting them before their eyes. And nothing is truer in describing their condition than what God said about them: 'As for those in whose hearts is deviation, they follow what is ambiguous of it, seeking discord and seeking its interpretation' (Āl ʿImrān 3:7).
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
This passage is a comparative analysis of the methodologies of the Salaf (early Muslims) and the Khalaf (later scholars) regarding the interpretation of divine attributes, followed by a strong condemnation of anthropomorphists. The author begins by stating that the Salaf's method was best for their time because it was most consonant with innate faith. The Khalaf's method became necessary due to intellectual challenges and the development of Arabic rhetorical sciences (balāghah) including metaphor (majāz), similitude (tashbīh), and allegory (istiʿārah). He provides the example of Imam Malik's response about al-istiwāʾ: accepting the term without asking 'how.' The Khalaf, however, had to analyze texts rhetorically because of heretics who demanded detailed explanations. Crucially, the author asserts that both methods lead to the same goal: affirming that God is unlike any creation and transcendent. Thus the difference is merely formal. Then he dismisses the deviant groups: the Muʿaṭṭilah (those who negate attributes) and the Mujassimah (anthropomorphists) who take literal meanings and ignore metaphorical language. He describes them as people who create mental idols and then force verses to support them, quoting Quran 3:7 as a description of their deviation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God has a physical form because the Quran describes His hands, face, etc.
Correction: The Quran uses metaphorical language; literal interpretation leads to anthropomorphism, which is condemned.

According to the passage, what is the main error of the Mujassimah?
A) They deny all attributes

Key Takeaway
Those who imagine God as a body or deny His attributes based on literal readings are outside the bounds of valid Quranic interpretation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The passage describes those who 'seek support from Quranic verses for their preconceived notions.' Can you identify a time when you approached the Quran looking for confirmation of your own ideas instead of letting it challenge and reshape your beliefs?
?
If your heart harbors even a small 'zig' (deviation) towards any of your own opinions about God, will you repent and return to the way of the righteous predecessors who accepted the texts as they came, without distorting their meanings?

Denial of Final Cause in Allah's Actions
Definition of final cause and partial proof that Allah's actions are not based on it.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the concept of final cause and why it cannot be attributed to Allah's actions due to the perfection of His will.

Core Idea
Allah's perfect will needs no external purpose; final causes imply need.

This lesson defines the concept of 'final cause'—a purpose that drives human actions—and then begins to show why such causes cannot apply to Allah. Since Allah's will is perfect and free from any compulsion, attributing final causes to His actions would imply that He is driven by need, which contradicts His perfection. The argument is introduced but concludes on the following page.

Guided Path
1
Understand the definition of final cause
Read the definition carefully: final cause is the purpose in the mind that drives one to take means. Note its two-stage existence: mental before, external after.
2
Examine the example
The example of seeking warmth and putting on a coat illustrates how human actions are driven by purposes. This makes the concept clear.
3
Consider the argument against final causes in Allah
The passage invokes Allah's perfect will (al-irāda) which is free from compulsion. If Allah's actions had final causes, it would mean He is compelled by need, which is impossible. The proof is cut off mid-sentence, but the reasoning is clear.
The argument continues on page 144, so you may need to consult the next lesson for the complete proof.

نفي العلة الغائية عن أفعاله جل جلاله

تعريف العلة الغائية :
ويقصد بالعلة الغائية ، الغرض الذي يقوم في ذهن الإنسان ويتجه إلى تحقيقه ، فيدفعه ذلك إلى تنفيذ الوسائل والأسباب التي توصله إلى ذلك الغرض . فالغرض الذي قام في ذهنه هو العلة لتحقيق تلك الوسائل والأسباب ، ومن أجل أن هذا الغرض هو في الحقيقة غاية يستهدفها الإنسان عند مباشرته الأسباب يطلق عليه العلماء اسم : العلة الغائية. ومن شأن هذه العلة أنها في الوجود الذهني تكون سابقة على القيام بالوسائل والأسباب وأما في الوجود الخارجي والحقيقي فتأتي متأخرة عنها .
مثال ذلك شعورك بالحاجة إلى الدفء . فإنه غرض يحملك على أن تقوم فترتدي معطفك الثقيل ، فإذا فعلت ذلك تحقق لك الغرض المطلوب وأخذت تشعر بالدفء ، فتحقيق الدفء علة غائية ، لأنها الحامل على الفعل ، وهي ماثلة في الذهن من قبله ولكنها تتحقق في الخارج بعده

• ولكن هل يمكن والحالة هذه أن نقول بأن أفعال الله تقوم على علل غـائـيـة كشأن أفعالنا نحن ؟..
والجواب أنه لا يجوز لنا أن نقول ذلك ، لأنه يتنافى مع ما ثبت من أن صفة الإرادة في ذاته سبحانه وتعالى صفة تامة كاملة وأنه لا يشوبها أي جبر أو قسر . فلو قلت بأن الله عز وجل أنزل المطر من أجل علة استهدفها ، وهو ظهور النبات على وجه الأرض ، وأنها هى الحاملة له على إنزال المطر ( كما هو شأن العلة الغائية ( فمعنى ذلك أنك تقول : إن الضرورة هي التي حملته على الإمطار ، إذ
Denial of final cause from His acts, majestic is His glory.

Definition of final cause:
By final cause is meant the purpose that arises in the human mind and which one aims to achieve, driving him to implement the means and causes that lead to that purpose. So the purpose that occurred in his mind is the cause for implementing those means and causes, and because this purpose is in reality a goal that man targets when undertaking the means, scholars call it the final cause. It is characteristic of this cause that in mental existence it precedes the undertaking of means and causes, whereas in external and real existence it occurs after them.
An example of that is your feeling of need for warmth. For it is a purpose that drives you to stand and put on your heavy coat, and when you do that, the desired purpose is realized and you begin to feel warmth. So achieving warmth is a final cause, because it is the impetus for the action, and it is present in the mind before it, but it is realized externally after it.

Explanation of the absence of final cause from the acts of Allah Almighty:
If you know this, we say:
• Firstly – We mentioned that among the established attributes of meanings for Allah Almighty is the attribute of will (al-irāda), and you have learned its meaning and that it negates compulsion and coercion to do what one does not will, and you have learned that the will of Allah Almighty is perfect, not tainted by any meaning of compulsion or forcing to do what He does not will. Thus, the will of Allah transcends the will of man, for it is in man imperfect and tainted by constraint and compulsion, but with respect to Allah Almighty it is perfect and complete. This is a clear fact that the researcher understands by reflection.

• But can we, in this state, say that Allah's acts are based on final causes like our acts?..
The answer is that we are not permitted to say that, because it contradicts what has been established that the attribute of will in His essence, glorified and exalted, is a perfect and complete attribute and that no compulsion or constraint taints it. For if you say that Allah Almighty sent down rain for a cause He aimed at, which is the appearance of vegetation on the face of the earth, and that it is what drove Him to send down rain (as is the case with final cause), then that means you are saying that necessity is what drove Him to send down rain, for
Source pages p. 143

Commentary
This passage is a definition and a proof regarding the denial of final cause (al-ʿilla al-ghāʾiyya) in Allah's actions. The author first defines the final cause as a purpose in the human mind that drives one to take means to achieve it, noting that it exists mentally before the action and externally after it. He gives the example of seeking warmth leading to putting on a coat. Then he transitions to showing that Allah's actions are not subject to final causes. He begins by recalling the attribute of will (al-irāda) in Allah, which is perfect and free from any compulsion or constraint, unlike human will which is imperfect and tainted. The argument then poses a question: can we say that Allah's acts have final causes like our acts? The answer is no, because that would imply that Allah is compelled by a need, contradicting the perfection of His will. The author illustrates with the example of rain: if one says Allah sent rain for the purpose of growing plants, that would mean necessity (al-ḍarūra) drove Him to send rain, which is not fitting for His perfection. The passage ends mid-argument; the conclusion is continued on the next page.

Key Terms
العلة الغائية
الإرادة
الجبر
القسر
الضرورة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That Allah's actions are motivated by purposes or goals like human actions.
Correction: Allah's will is perfect and self-sufficient; He does not act out of need or to achieve a goal. Attributing final causes to Allah implies imperfection in His will.

Checkpoint
What is the main reason the author gives for denying final causes in Allah's actions?
A) Because final causes only apply to inanimate objects.
B) Because it would imply that Allah's will is imperfect and subject to compulsion.
C) Because the Quran explicitly denies them.
D) Because scholars have never used the term.

Key Takeaway
Allah's will is perfect and self-sufficient, so His actions are not driven by external purposes; final causes belong only to imperfect human actions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a difficult trial, do you find yourself secretly demanding to know the reason why? This lesson shows that Allah's will is perfect and needs no external purpose. Are you willing to submit to His decree without requiring an explanation? What concrete step can you take today to surrender that demand?
?
Your own will is often driven by needs and purposes. In what area of your life are you planning as if your will is sufficient, forgetting your total dependence on Allah? How can you realign your intentions to flow from submission to His perfect will, not from your own agenda?
?
This lesson teaches that attaching a final cause to Allah's actions would imply necessity and imperfection. Have you ever thought of Allah's actions as having 'reasons' in the same way human actions do? What does this reveal about your understanding of His transcendence? Will you commit to reflecting on His names and attributes to deepen your awe and trust?

On the Impossibility of Final Causes in God's Actions
Buti argues that God's actions cannot have final causes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why attributing final causes (al-ʿilla al-ghāʾiyya) to God's actions is incompatible with His perfect will, absolute power, and utter perfection.

Core Idea
God's actions need no purpose; final causes imply deficiency and contradict His perfection.

This passage tackles a subtle but critical point: even though human actions are goal-driven, we cannot project that onto God. Buti systematically demonstrates that final causes would taint God's perfect will with necessity, contradict His absolute power by requiring intermediaries, and imply imperfection. Let's examine his three-fold argument.

Guided Path
1
Understand the concept of final cause
Start with the human example: feeling cold impels you to put on a coat; achieving warmth is the final cause. Notice that it exists in the mind before the action and in reality after.
This sets the stage for why such a cause cannot apply to God.
2
Follow the first argument: perfect will
Buti recalls that God's will is perfect, free from compulsion. If we say God acts for a purpose (e.g., rain for plants), that implies necessity taints His will, which is kufr.
3
Follow the second argument: absolute power
God's absolute power means He creates directly without intermediaries. Final causes would introduce means between God's power and the effect, contradicting Qur'anic assertions of direct creation.
4
Consider the third argument: divine perfection
From His negative and positive attributes, God is all-perfect. Final causes are needed by deficient agents; attributing them to God would imply imperfection, which is impossible.
This argument is cut off in the source but the point is clear.
5
Reflect on the implication
Attributing final causes to God is not just a mistake but pure disbelief (kufr), as it contradicts the very meaning of divinity.

مثال ذلك شعورك بالحاجة إلى الدفء . فإنه غرض يحملك على أن تقوم فترتدي معطفك الثقيل ، فإذا فعلت ذلك تحقق لك الغرض المطلوب وأخذت تشعر بالدفء ، فتحقيق الدفء علة غائية ، لأنها الحامل على الفعل ، وهي ماثلة في الذهن من قبله ولكنها تتحقق في الخارج بعده .
بيان انتفاء العلة الغائية عن أفعال الله تعالى :
إذا علمت هذا ، نقول :
أولاً - ذكرنا أن من جملة صفات المعاني الثابتة لله تعالى ، صفة الإرادة وقد علمت معناها وأنها تنافي الجبر والإكراه على فعل ما لا يريد كما علمت أن إرادة الله تعالى تامة لا يشوبها أي معنى من معاني الجبر والحمل على ما لا يريد . وبذلك تترق إرادة الله عن إرادة الإنسان ، فهي في الإنسان ناقصة مشوبة بالقسر والجبر ، ولكنها بالنسبة لله عز وجل تامة كاملة . وهذه حقيقة واضحة يفهمها الباحث بتأمل . ولكن هل يمكن والحالة هذه أن نقول بأن أفعال الله تقوم على علل غائية كشأن أفعالنا نحن ؟.. والجواب أنه لا يجوز لنا أن نقول ذلك ، لأنه يتنافى مع ما ثبت من أن صفة الإرادة في ذاته سبحانه وتعالى صفة تامة كاملة وأنه لا يشوبها أي جبر أو قسر . فلو قلت بأن الله عز وجل أنزل المطر من أجل علة استهدفها ، وهو ظهور النبات على وجه الأرض ، وأنها هي الحاملة له على إنزال المطر ( كما هو شأن العلة الغائية ) فمعنى ذلك أنك تقول : إن الضرورة هي التي حملته على الإمطار ، إذ كانت هي الوسيلة الوحيدة التي لا بدَّ منها للنبات . فالإرادة الكاملة متجهة إذاً إلى الإنبات ، أما إلى الإمطار فإنها مشوبة بقدر كبير من الضرورة التي تنافي الإرادة . وكذلك القول بالنسبة لجميع المخلوقات التي هي أسباب غيرها . ومعلوم أن مثل هذا الاعتقاد أو القول في حق الباري جل جلاله ، كفر محض وأنه يتناقض مع مقتضى الألوهية تناقضاً بيناً .
ثانياً - ذكرنا أن من صفاته أيضاً القدرة التامة المطلقة وهي تستلزم أن يكون جميع الموجودات بخلقه وتكوينه ، وإلا لما صدقت صفة القدرة التامة المطلقة بالنسبة إليه جل جلاله . على أن القرآن قد صرح في أكثر من موطن بأن جميع الموجودات من خلقه . كقوله عز وجل ﴿ وَخَلَقَ كُلَّ شَيْءٍ فَقَدَّرَهُ تَقْدِيرًا ﴾ [ الفرقان : ٢ ] وقوله ﴿ هو الذي خَلَقَ لَكُمْ ما في الأرض جميعاً ﴾ [ البقرة : ٢٩ ] وقوله ﴿ أَوَلَمْ يَرَوا أنَّ الله الذي خلق السموات والأرض قادر على أن يخلق مِثْلَهُمْ ﴾ [الإسراء : ٩٩ ] . وإنما يصدق أن الله عز وجل قد خلق كل شيء ، إذا توجهت إليه قدرته ابتداء بدون اتخاذ أي واسطة أو سبب ، وكان وجوده بسبب مباشر واحد ، هو قدرة الله وخلقه . فأما إذا قدرنا العلة الغائية في أفعاله وخلقه ، فمعنى ذلك أن بين قدرة الله عز وجل وبين تلك العلة وسائل وأسباباً هي المؤثر المباشر في إيجاد الغاية ، فلم يتعلق خلق الله بها إلا عن طريق التوسط والتسبب إليها . وهو مناف لتلك النصوص القرآنية التي تنطق في عبارة قاطعة بأن الله هو الخالق المباشر لكل شيء كما أنه مناف لاتصاف الله تعالى بالقدرة المطلقة .
ثالثاً - علمت من مجموع ما ذكرناه من الصفات السلبية وصفات المعاني والمعنوية أن الله عز وجل متصف بكل صفات الكمال ومنزه عن كل صفات النقص . فلو قلنا مع ذلك بأن أفعال الله عز وجل تنطوي على العلة الغائية كما
An example of that is your feeling of need for warmth. For it is a purpose that drives you to get up and put on your heavy coat, and when you do that, the desired purpose is achieved and you begin to feel warmth. So achieving warmth is a final cause, because it is what impels the action, and it is present in the mind before it, but it is realized in the external world after it.
Statement of the absence of the final cause from the actions of Allah Almighty:
If you know this, we say:
Firstly – we mentioned that among the attributes of meanings (ṣifāt al-maʿānī) established for Allah Almighty is the attribute of will (al-irāda), and you know its meaning and that it negates compulsion (al-jabr) and coercion (al-ikrāh) to do what one does not will, as you know that the will of Allah Almighty is perfect, not tainted by any meaning of compulsion or impellent to what He does not will. Thus the will of Allah transcends the will of man, for it is in man deficient and mixed with constraint and compulsion, but with respect to Allah Almighty it is perfect and complete. And this is a clear truth that the researcher understands through contemplation. But can we, in this state, say that the actions of Allah are based on final causes like our actions? The answer is that we are not permitted to say that, because it conflicts with what has been established that the attribute of will in His Essence, glorified and exalted, is a perfect and complete attribute, and that no compulsion or constraint taints it. For if you said that Allah Almighty sent down rain for a purpose He intended, namely the emergence of plants on the face of the earth, and that it is what impelled Him to send down rain (as is the case with final cause), then that means you are saying: necessity is what compelled Him to send down rain, since it is the sole necessary means for plants. So the perfect will is directed towards causing plants to grow, while regarding sending down rain it is tainted by a great deal of necessity that contradicts will. And the same applies to all created things that are causes for others. And it is known that such a belief or statement concerning the Creator, may His majesty be exalted, is pure disbelief (kufr) and clearly contradicts the requirements of divinity.
Secondly – we mentioned that among His attributes is also absolute perfect power (al-qudra al-tāmma al-muṭlaqa), which necessitates that all existent things are by His creation and bringing into being, otherwise the attribute of absolute perfect power would not be true with respect to Him, may His majesty be exalted. Moreover, the Qur'an has declared in more than one place that all existent things are from His creation, such as His saying, exalted be He, {And He created everything and determined it with precise determination} [Al-Furqan: 2], and His saying {It is He who created for you all that is on the earth} [Al-Baqara: 29], and His saying {Do they not see that Allah, who created the heavens and the earth, is able to create the like of them?} [Al-Isra': 99]. And it is only true that Allah Almighty has created everything if His power is directed to it initially without adopting any intermediary or cause, and its existence is by one direct cause, which is Allah's power and creation. But if we posit a final cause in His actions and creation, that means that between the power of Allah Almighty and that cause there are means and causes that are the direct effectors in bringing about the purpose, so His creation is not related to it except through mediation and causation. This contradicts those Qur'anic texts that speak in decisive terms that Allah is the direct creator of everything, and it also contradicts Allah Almighty being described with absolute power.
Thirdly – you have known from the totality of what we have mentioned of the negative attributes (al-ṣifāt al-salbiyya) and the attributes of meanings (ṣifāt al-maʿānī) and the relational attributes (al-maʿnawiyya) that Allah Almighty is described with all attributes of perfection and is transcendent above all attributes of deficiency. So if we say, despite that, that the actions of Allah Almighty involve the final cause, as...
Source pages p. 143

Commentary
This passage is a proof (bayān) that final causes (al-ʿilla al-ghāʾiyya) do not apply to God's actions. It begins with a human example to clarify the concept: feeling cold impels one to put on a coat; achieving warmth is the final cause, existing in the mind before the action and in reality after it. Then the author builds a three-part argument.

First, he recalls the attribute of will (al-irāda) as established for God. God's will is perfect, free from any compulsion or coercion, unlike human will which is deficient and mixed with necessity. If we claimed God acts for a final cause—e.g., sending rain for the purpose of plant growth—then we imply that necessity (to produce plants) compelled Him to send rain. This taints His perfect will with necessity, which is pure disbelief (kufr) and contradicts divinity.

Second, he refers to the attribute of absolute power (al-qudra al-muṭlaqa). This power requires that all things exist directly by God's creation without intermediaries. The Qur'an asserts God created everything directly. If we posit a final cause, that implies there are means and causes between God's power and the effect, making Him create through mediation, contradicting His absolute power and the clear Qur'anic texts.

Third, he summarizes that from the negative attributes (ṣifāt salbiyya), attributes of meanings (ṣifāt maʿānī), and relational attributes (ṣifāt maʿnawiyya), God is all-perfect and free from any deficiency. To attribute a final cause to His actions would imply deficiency, because final causes are needed by deficient agents who lack something. (The third point is cut off, but the conclusion is clear: final causes are incompatible with God's perfection.)

Thus, the passage systematically refutes the notion of final causes in God's actions, showing it contradicts His perfect will, absolute power, and utter perfection.

Key Terms
علة غائية
إرادة
قدرة مطلقة
صفات المعاني
صفات سلبية
صفات معنوية
جبر
قسر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Since human actions have purposes, God's actions must also have purposes.
Correction: This passage shows that human purposes stem from need and deficiency, whereas God is absolutely perfect and self-sufficient. Attributing purposes to God would imply He is compelled by needs, contradicting His perfect will and power.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is it invalid to attribute final causes (al-ʿilla al-ghāʾiyya) to God's actions?
A) Because God does not will anything.
B) Because final causes would taint God's perfect will with necessity and imply intermediaries, contradicting His absolute power.
C) Because the Qur'an does not mention final causes.
D) Because final causes only exist in human actions, not in divine actions.

Key Takeaway
Attributing final causes to God contradicts His perfect will, absolute power, and transcendence, and constitutes disbelief.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face trials or unanswered prayers, do you find yourself inventing a hidden purpose for God's action to feel better? What does that reveal about your heart's need to justify God rather than submit to His perfect will?
?
If you truly believed that God's actions are free from any external goal or necessity, would it change how you react to events that seem pointless or unfair? Will you surrender the demand to see a purpose and instead trust His perfect will?
?
This lesson declares that attributing any purpose to God is pure disbelief. Have you ever thought of God's actions as 'for your benefit' as a primary cause? How can you purify your heart from this subtle form of limiting God's transcendence starting today?

Refuting Final Cause from Divine Will
The author argues that final causes contradict Allah's perfect will.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why attributing final causes to Allah contradicts His perfect will and constitutes disbelief.

Core Idea
Allah's will is perfect and free from necessity, so final causes cannot be attributed to Him.

This passage from Ramadan al-Buti tackles a subtle theological error: thinking that Allah's actions are mediated by final causes like those in nature. The author argues that such a view mixes Allah's perfect will with necessity, which is impermissible. Let's examine his argument closely.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Note the key terms: الإرادة (will), الضرورة (necessity), العلة الغائية (final cause).
Pay attention to the logical flow: the author moves from a specific example to a general rule.
2
Identify the hypothetical scenario
The author presents an example: if Allah's will were directed to rain as a means to grow plants, then that will would be mixed with necessity because rain is a necessary cause for plants.
Why is necessity problematic? Because perfect will must be free from any compulsion or dependency.
3
Generalize to all creatures as causes
The author extends the same reasoning to all creatures that act as intermediate causes for other things. This shows the principle is universal.
Think about any causal chain: what does it imply about Allah's will if He must use intermediaries?
4
Understand the theological conclusion
The author concludes that such a belief is pure disbelief (kufr) because it contradicts the very nature of divinity (al-ulūhiyya).
This is a strong statement. Reflect on why it's so severe.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كانت هي ألوان الواسطة التي لا بدَّ منها للنبات فالإرادة الكاملة متجهة إذاً إلى الإنبات، أما إلى الإمطار فإنها مشوبة بقدر كبير من الضرورة التي تنافي الإرادة. وكذلك القول بالنسبة لجميع المخلوقات التي هي أسباب غيرها. ومعلوم أن مثل هذا الاعتقاد أو القول في حق الباري جل جلاله، كفر محض وأنه يتناقض مع مقتضى الألوهية تناقضاً بيناً.
They were the types of intermediate [cause] that are necessary for plants; so the perfect will is directed to growth, but as for rain, it is mixed with a great amount of necessity which contradicts will. And the same applies to all creatures that are causes for others. And it is known that such a belief or statement regarding the Exalted and Glorious One is pure disbelief and clearly contradicts the requirements of divinity.
Source pages p. 144

Commentary
This passage is an argument against attributing final causes (al-illa al-ghā'iyya) to Allah's actions, specifically focusing on the attribute of will (al-irāda). The author presents a hypothetical: if Allah's will were directed to causing rain as a means to grow plants, then that will would be mixed with necessity (ḍarūra) because rain is a necessary cause. True perfect will must be free from any necessity. Therefore, Allah's will is directly toward the final effect (growth) without intermediate means. The author then generalizes to all creatures that act as causes, concluding that believing Allah acts through such final causes constitutes pure disbelief (kufr) because it contradicts the essence of divinity (al-ulūhiyya).

Key Terms

الضرورة (al-ḍarūra)
العلة الغائية (al-illa al-ghā'iyya)
الكفر (al-kufr)
الألوهية (al-ulūhiyya)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Thinking that Allah's will can be dependent on created means without compromising His perfection.
Correction: Allah's perfect will must be free from any necessity or dependency on intermediate causes. Attributing final causes to Him implies such necessity, which contradicts His divinity and constitutes disbelief.

Checkpoint
According to the text, why is attributing final causes to Allah considered disbelief?
A) Because it implies Allah has needs
B) Because it contradicts His perfect will by mixing it with necessity
C) Because it denies the existence of causes
D) Because it anthropomorphizes Allah

Key Takeaway
Final causes imply necessity, which contradicts Allah's perfect will and thus constitutes disbelief.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever, even in passing, thought that Allah does something 'because' of a created cause, as if He were forced to respond? How does this lesson expose that thought as a seed of disbelief? Repent and affirm His perfect will tonight.
?
When you make dua, do you expect that your prayer is a necessary means for Allah's action? How does the perfect freedom of His will in this lesson liberate you from making your supplication a condition, and instead worship Him as absolutely independent?
?
Read the last line of the passage again: 'pure disbelief.' Is there any hidden assumption in your heart that Allah's actions are driven by needs or purposes similar to yours? Bring that assumption before Him now and ask forgiveness for reducing His majesty to human limitations.

Proof from Absolute Power: Allah's Direct Creation
Proof from absolute power for direct creation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Allah's attribute of absolute power necessitates that all things are created directly by Him without intermediaries or secondary causes.

Core Idea
Absolute power means direct creation; no intermediaries can exist.

This lesson examines a key proof in Islamic theology: that Allah's absolute power requires direct creation of all things. The author argues that accepting secondary causes undermines the absoluteness of divine power and contradicts clear Qur'anic verses. We will explore the logical necessity and scriptural evidence for this doctrine.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Let the author's argument unfold naturally before analyzing.
Notice the author begins with the attribute of absolute power.
2
Identify the logical implication
The author states that absolute power necessitates that all existents are directly created by Allah. Ask yourself: why would indirect creation contradict absolute power?
3
Examine the Qur'anic evidence
Three verses are cited. Read each one and see how they support the claim that Allah created everything directly.
Verses: Al-Furqan 2, Al-Baqarah 29, Al-Isra 99.
4
Understand the rejection of final causes
The author argues that assuming final causes (ends) in Allah's actions would introduce intermediaries, contradicting absolute power. Reflect on why this is problematic.
Final causes imply means to achieve them, which would be intermediaries.
5
Reflect on the implications for tawheed
Consider why this proof is important: it reinforces that Allah alone is the direct creator and sustainer, with no partners or secondary agents.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثانياً - ذكرنا أن من صفاته أيضاً القدرة التامة المطلقة وهي تستلزم أن يكون جميع الموجودات بخلقه وتكوينه، وإلا لما صدقت صفة القدرة التامة المطلقة بالنسبة إليه جل جلاله. على أن القرآن قد صرح في أكثر من موطن بأن جميع الموجودات من خلقه. كقوله عز وجل ﴿ وَخَلَقَ كُلَّ شَيْءٍ فَقَدَّرَهُ تَقْدِيرًا ﴾ [ الفرقان : ٢ ] وقوله هو الذي خَلَقَ لَكُمْ ما في الأرض جميعاً ﴾ [ البقرة : ٢٩] وقوله ﴿ أوَلَمْ يَرَوا أنَّ الله الذي خلق السموات والأرض قادر على أن يخلق مِثْلَهُمْ ﴾ [الإسراء : ٩٩ ] . وإنما يصدق أن الله عز وجل قد خلق كل شيء، إذا توجهت إليه قدرته ابتداء بدون اتخاذ أي واسطة أو سبب، وكان وجوده بسبب مباشر واحد، هو قدرة الله وخلقه. فأما إذا قدرنا العلة الغائية في أفعاله وخلقه، فمعنى ذلك أن بين قدرة الله عز وجل وبين تلك العلة وسائل وأسباباً هي المؤثر المباشر في إيجاد الغاية، فلم يتعلق خلق الله بها إلا عن طريق التوسط والتسبب إليها. وهو مناف لتلك النصوص القرآنية التي تنطق في عبارة قاطعة بأن الله هو الخالق المباشر لكل شيء كما أنه مناف لاتصاف الله تعالى بالقدرة المطلقة.
Secondly – we mentioned that among His attributes is also absolute complete power, and it necessitates that all existents are by His creation and formation; otherwise the attribute of absolute complete power would not be verified with respect to Him, Exalted and Glorious. Moreover, the Qur'an has stated in more than one place that all existents are from His creation, such as His saying, Exalted and Majestic: {And He created everything and determined it with [precise] determination} [Al-Furqan: 2], and His saying: {He it is who created for you all that is on the earth} [Al-Baqarah: 29], and His saying: {Do they not see that Allah, who created the heavens and the earth, is able to create the likes of them?} [Al-Isra: 99]. And it is only true that Allah, Exalted and Glorious, has created everything if His power is directed to it initially without taking any intermediary or cause, and its existence is by one direct cause, which is the power and creation of Allah. But if we assume final causes in His actions and creation, that means that between the power of Allah, Exalted and Glorious, and that final cause there are means and causes that are the direct influencer in bringing about the end, so Allah's creation is not connected to them except by way of mediation and causation. This contradicts those Qur'anic texts that speak in decisive terms that Allah is the direct creator of everything, and it also contradicts Allah's being described with absolute power.
Source pages p. 144

Commentary
This passage is a proof from the attribute of absolute power (al-qudra al-muṭlaqa) for the directness of Allah's creation. The author argues that absolute power necessitates that all existents are directly created by Allah; otherwise, the attribute would not be truly absolute. He supports this with three Qur'anic verses stating that Allah created everything. The key point is that Allah's power must be directed to each thing directly, without intermediaries. If we postulate final causes, then there would be means between Allah's power and the effect, making the power indirect and thus not absolute. Therefore, attributing final causes to Allah's actions contradicts both the Qur'anic verses and the attribute of absolute power.

الخلق المباشر (al-khalq al-mubāshir)
العلة الغائية (al-illa al-ghā'iyya)
التوسط (al-tawassuṭ)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Allah's power can be expressed through secondary causes without diminishing its absoluteness.
Correction: The author argues that absolute power requires direct creation; secondary causes would make the power indirect and thus not truly absolute.

Checkpoint

C) That Allah's power is limited to certain actions

Key Takeaway
Allah's absolute power demands that He is the direct creator of everything, leaving no room for independent secondary causes or intermediaries.

?

Why Allah's Actions Cannot Have Final Causes
An argument that final causes imply imperfection in Allah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why attributing final causes to Allah's actions contradicts His absolute perfection.

Core Idea
Final causes imply need, which contradicts Allah's perfection.

In the previous lessons, we established that Allah possesses all attributes of perfection and is free from any deficiency. Now, we turn to a crucial implication: if Allah's actions had final causes—like human actions seeking goals—that would introduce need and deficiency into His nature. Read the following passage carefully to see how the author argues this point.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the strong conclusion: 'فكيف يصح أن تستند هذه العلة إلى شيء من أفعال الخالق'
2
Identify the two aspects of deficiency
The passage lists two specific ways a being is deficient if it relies on a final cause. Find both and note how they are described.
3
Understand the logical contradiction
Connect the two aspects of deficiency to the earlier established fact that Allah is absolutely perfect. Why does this create a contradiction?
The author uses the word 'لأن' to explain the reasoning.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
The author ends with a rhetorical question. What is the implied answer? How does this protect Allah's transcendence?
This question summarizes the entire argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثالثاً - علمت من مجموع ما ذكرناه من الصفات السلبية وصفات المعاني والمعنوية أن الله عز وجل متصف بكل صفات الكمال ومنزه عن كل صفات النقص. فلو قلنا مع ذلك بأن أفعال الله عز وجل تنطوي على العلة الغائية كما هو الشأن بالنسبة لنا، لاستلزم ذلك القول بأن الله عز وجل متصف ببعض النقائص وأنه يستكمل هذه النقائص بغيره، تعالى الله عن ذلك علواً كبيراً. لأن من يحتاج إلى أمر ثم لا يستطيع بلوغ هذا الأمر إلا بواسطة معينة يستعملها فإنما ناقص من جهتين : الأولى من حيث إنه يحتاج إلى ذلك الأمر، والحاجة فرع من النقص، والثانية من حيث إنه لم يقدر أن يصل إليه إلا مستعيناً بغيره. فهذا شأن كل من تقوم أعماله على أساس العلة الغائية. فكيف يصح أن تستند هذه العلة إلى شيء من أفعال الخالق جل جلاله ؟!
Thirdly – you have learned from the totality of what we mentioned of the negative attributes and the attributes of meanings and of the meaning-related that Allah, Exalted and Glorious, is characterized by all attributes of perfection and is free from all attributes of deficiency. So if we nevertheless say that the actions of Allah, Exalted and Glorious, involve the final cause as is the case with us, that would necessitate saying that Allah, Exalted and Glorious, is characterized by some deficiencies and that He perfects these deficiencies by others – exalted be Allah above that, greatly. Because whoever needs something and then cannot attain that thing except by a certain means that he uses is deficient in two respects: the first is that he needs that thing, and need is a branch of deficiency; the second is that he cannot reach it except by seeking help from others. This is the case of everyone whose actions are based on the final cause. So how can it be correct that this cause be attributed to anything from the actions of the Creator, Exalted and Glorious?!
Source pages p. 145

Commentary
This passage is an argument from Allah's absolute perfection (al-kamāl) against the attribution of final causes (al-illa al-ghā'iyya) to His actions. The author begins by reminding that from the negative attributes (ṣifāt salbiyya) and attributes of meanings (ṣifāt al-ma‘ānī) and meaning-related (ṣifāt ma‘nawiyya), we know Allah is perfect and free from all deficiency. If His actions had final causes like human actions, that would imply deficiency: He would need something and would have to use a means to achieve it. The author identifies two aspects of deficiency: (1) need itself, which is a branch of deficiency, and (2) inability to attain without external assistance. Since Allah is perfect, He cannot have such needs. Therefore, final causes cannot apply to Him.

Key Terms
الصفات السلبية (al-ṣifāt al-salbiyya)
صفات المعاني (ṣifāt al-ma‘ānī)
الكمال (al-kamāl)
النقص (al-naqṣ)
العلة الغائية (al-illa al-ghā'iyya)
الحاجة (al-ḥāja)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Assuming that final causes in human actions are analogous to divine actions, ignoring the imperfection they imply.
Correction: Human actions involve final causes because humans are inherently needy and imperfect. Allah is absolutely perfect and self-sufficient, so His actions cannot have final causes.

Checkpoint
According to the text, how many aspects of deficiency are involved in needing a final cause?
A) One
B) Two
C) Three
D) Four

Key Takeaway
Attributing final causes to Allah's actions would imply need and deficiency, contradicting His absolute perfection.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever find yourself acting for the sake of recognition or reward, even in your worship? The source shows that even the slightest hint of 'final cause' in Allah's actions would be a deficiency. How does this challenge your own motivation in your relationship with Allah? What is one action this week you will purify from any expectation of return?
?
When you think about why Allah created you, do you subconsciously assume He needed you or your worship? The source states that need is a branch of deficiency. How does this reshape your understanding of your own existence? Write down one concrete way you will remind yourself daily that Allah is absolutely self-sufficient.
?
The source says that whoever acts for a final cause is deficient in two ways: need and dependence on others. Can you identify an area of your life where you are acting primarily for a final cause (e.g., seeking approval, avoiding punishment)? How would reorienting that action purely for Allah's sake reflect the lesson's truth about divine perfection?

Proof from Qur'anic Creation and Guidance
Citing Qur'anic verses to negate final causes in divine action.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how two key Qur'anic verses establish that Allah directly creates and guides all things, with no independent causality or final causes in His actions.

Core Idea
Allah directly creates and guides; no cause exists except by His will.

In this passage, the author reinforces the rational arguments against final causes in Allah's actions with clear scriptural evidence. Two powerful Qur'anic verses are presented as explicit, decisive texts that every cause in the universe is created and made by Allah alone. Studying these verses will deepen your appreciation for how revelation confirms reason on this fundamental point of divine transcendence.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the full Arabic passage once without analyzing, then the English translation. Notice how the author presents the verses as 'explicit decisive texts' (نص صريح قاطع).
The verses are from Surah Ta-Ha and Surah Al-A‘la.
2
Identify the two Qur'anic verses
Locate the two verses cited. For each, note the key phrases: 'أَعْطى كُلَّ شَيءٍ خَلْقَهُ ثُمَّ هَدى' and 'خَلَقَ فَسَوَّى ... قَدَّرَ فَهَدى'. What do they attribute to Allah?
Both verses pair creation (خلق) with guidance (هدى).
3
Understand the author's inference
After quoting the verses, the author states: 'This is an explicit decisive text that there is no cause in the universe except by His creation and making.' Reflect on how the verses lead to this conclusion.
The key is that both the essence (creation) and the causality (guidance) come directly from Allah.
4
Reflect on the rhetorical question
The author asks: 'How could it be imagined that this Great Creator would make some of His creatures intermediaries to achieve specific ends?' Consider why this is impossible based on the verses.
If all causality is from Allah, intermediaries become redundant.
5
Connect to the concept of final cause
The passage ends by stating that reflecting on this will help you grasp the meaning of 'final cause' (العلة الغائية) and why it cannot apply to Allah's actions. Review how this connects to the broader discussion of divine attributes.
Final cause implies a goal extrinsic to the agent, which is incompatible with Allah's self-sufficiency.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
رابعاً ـ ذكر الله في كتابه العظيم في بيان مشرق معجز، أنه سبحانه خلق كل شيء مما تراه موجوداً، وبث فيه عمله الذي أراده له، أي خلق الذات وأعطاها السببية أيضاً لما شاء من المسببات فقال : ﴿ قالَ رَبُّنَا الَّذي أَعْطى كُلَّ شَيءٍ خَلْقَهُ ثُمَّ هَدى ﴾ [ طه : ٥٠] وقال ﴿ سَبِّح اسْمَ رَبِّكَ الأغلى الَّذي خَلَقَ فَسَوَّى والذي قَدَّرَ فَهَدى ﴾ [ الأعلى : ١ - ٣ ] وهذا نص صريح قاطع بأن لا سبب في الكون إلا بخلقه وجعله، فكيف يتصور مع ذلك أن يوسط هذا الخالق العظيم بعض مخلوقاته لتحقيق غايات معينة ؟!. فإذا تأملت في هذا الذي ذكرناه أدركت جيداً معنى العلة الغائية ومعنى أن الله تعالى لا يمكن أن يتصف شيء من أفعاله بها، واستيقنت ذلك بالأدلة العقلية والنقلية التي أوضحناها.
Fourthly – Allah mentioned in His Mighty Book in a brilliant miraculous statement that He, glorified, created everything that you see existing, and infused in it the action that He willed for it, i.e., He created the essence and gave it causality also for whatever He willed of effects. He said: {They said: Our Lord is He who gave everything its creation, then guided} [Ta-Ha: 50], and He said: {Glorify the name of your Lord, the Most High, who created and proportioned, and who determined and guided} [Al-A‘la: 1-3]. This is an explicit decisive text that there is no cause in the universe except by His creation and making. So how could it be imagined, after that, that this Great Creator would make some of His creatures intermediaries to achieve specific ends?! So if you reflect on what we have mentioned, you will fully grasp the meaning of the final cause and the meaning that Allah, Exalted, cannot have any of His actions characterized by it, and you will be certain of that by the rational and transmitted proofs we have clarified.
Source pages p. 145

Commentary
This passage provides a scriptural argument against final causes in Allah's actions. The author cites two Qur'anic verses: (1) 'Our Lord is He who gave everything its creation, then guided' (Ta-Ha: 50) and (2) 'Glorify the name of your Lord, the Most High, who created and proportioned, and who determined and guided' (Al-A‘la: 1-3). The key point is that Allah directly gives each thing its creation (khalq) and then guides it (hudā). This shows that He is responsible for both the essence and the causality (sababiyya) of things. Therefore, there is no cause in the universe except by Allah's creation and making. Hence, the idea of Allah using creatures as intermediaries to achieve ends is impossible. The author concludes by inviting reflection, asserting that these rational and transmitted proofs establish the meaning of final cause and that it cannot be attributed to Allah's actions.

Key Terms
العلة الغائية (al-illa al-ghā'iyya)
السببية (al-sababiyya)
الخلق (al-khalq)
الهدى (al-hudā)
الأدلة العقلية والنقلية (al-adilla al-‘aqliyya wa al-naqliyya)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Misinterpreting verses that seem to attribute causality to created things as implying independence from Allah.
Correction: The verses explicitly show that Allah gives everything its creation and guidance, meaning all causality is directly from Him, not independently from creatures.

Checkpoint
What do the verses 'He gave everything its creation, then guided' and 'He created and proportioned, determined and guided' prove?
A) That created things act independently
B) That there is no cause in the universe except by Allah's creation and making
C) That final causes are necessary for understanding divine action
D) That guidance is separate from creation

Key Takeaway
Allah directly creates and guides everything; no cause in the universe exists except by His creation and making.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think about something you 'achieve' in your daily life, do you truly attribute its cause directly to Allah as this lesson demands, or do you unconsciously credit your own efforts or other intermediaries? What would it look like to consistently affirm that Allah is the sole creator and giver of causality in every outcome?
?
The verse says Allah gave everything its creation and then guided it. Have you ever reflected on the guidance Allah has given specifically to you—not just in religious matters, but in the very functioning of your body, your talents, your circumstances? How would your gratitude change if you saw every ability as a direct gift of causality from Him?
?
Consider the rhetorical question in the passage: How could it be imagined that Allah would make intermediaries to achieve ends? Are there areas of your life where you act as if Allah 'needs' your actions or others' to accomplish His will, rather than seeing you as a direct instrument of His creation? What step can you take today to realign your trust in His direct causation?

Good and Evil Are Conventional Because God Is the Direct Creator
Buti argues that God's direct creation entails conventional morality.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Ash'ari position holds that good and evil are not intrinsic qualities of actions but are conventional judgments created by God.

Core Idea
If God creates everything, then nothing is good or evil by its own essence.

This lesson presents the foundational argument for the Ash'ari view that moral values are not inherent in actions but are bestowed by God. The logic flows from God's absolute creative power: since God directly creates all things including their qualities, the goodness or badness of an act cannot be an essential property. Instead, it is a conventional attribution that depends on God's decree.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and title
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Notice that the title states the conclusion: nothing is obligatory upon God, and good/evil are conventional.
The title is programmatic, not yet argued.
2
Understand the logical link
Identify how Buti connects the previous truth (no intermediary between God and creation) to the conclusion. He argues that if God creates everything directly, then things cannot inherently contain good or evil.
The phrase 'انطواء ذاتياً' means inherent inclusion.
3
Grasp the meaning of 'conventional'
Buti explains that good and evil are meanings that follow God's ruling (hukm), not essential roots in the thing. He emphasizes that God could reverse them if He willed.
This leads to the statement: 'وهذا معنى قولنا: إن الحسن والقبح في الأشياء اعتباري'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
☆ ٣ - لا يجب على الله شيء والحسن والقبح في الأشياء اعتباري لعلك تدرك إذا تأملت في هذا العنوان ، أنه نتيجة ضرورية للحقيقة السابقة التي أوضحناها . فإذا ثبت أنه لا واسطة بين الله وخلق أي شيء مما تعلقت إرادته بخلقه ، وأن كل الموجودات بما فيها من تكيف وأعراض إنما هو بخلق مباشر من الله - فقد ثبت إذاً أن الأشياء لا تنطوي انطواء ذاتياً على شيء من الحسن والقبح ، أي لا يمكن أن تكون متسمة بحسن أو قبح ، متأصلين فيها بالطبع لا بالخلق . فخالقيـة الله لجميع الأشياء بجميع صفاتها ، تقتضي أن يكون هو الخالق للشيء ، وهو الخالق لمعنى الحسن ولمعنى القبح ثم هو الرابط والجامع بين ذلك الشيء وهذا المعنى . وإذا أدركت هذه الحقيقة ، أدركت إلى جانب ذلك أن الحسن أو القبح ليس له جذور ذاتية مرتبطة بذات الشيء بحيث لا يمكن الانفكاك عنه ، وإنما هو معنى استتبع حكماً من أحكام الله عز وجل ، فكان مانسميه نحن بالحسن أو القبح ، ولو شاء الله لعكس الأمر فجعل الحسن قبيحاً والقبيح حسنـاً ، مادام الكل بخلق الله وحكمه ، وهذا معنى قولنا : إن الحسن والقبح في الأشياء اعتباري . ولعلك تعجب فتقول : كيف أفهم أن حسن الصدق والعدل اعتباري وليس بذاتي فيه ، أو أن قبح الكذب والظلم اعتباري وليس بذاتي فيه ؟! فالجواب : أن الحسن أو القبح في مثل هذه الأمور ينبع من عدة نواح كلها اعتبارية وخارجة عن ذات هذه الأمور وجوهرها ، فحسن الصدق إما أن يكون منبعثاً من أنه يجر إلى فوائد مختلفة تتحقق للصادق ، وإما من حيث إنه يثاب عليه يوم القيامة ، وإما من حيث إن النفوس جبلت على احترام الصادق والاشمئزاز من الكاذب ، وكلها - كما تجد - بواعث خارجة عن ذات الصدق نفسه . وهذا يعني أن الله كان ولا يزال قادراً على تحويل النفوس وطبائعها فلا تتعلق بحب الصدق ولا تشمئز من الكذب . وكذلك القول في مبادئ العدل مثلاً ، فنحن إنما نعدها أمراً حسناً من أجل أنها إنما تضمن لكل ذي حق حقه ، علة ، وهي خارجة عن ذات ذلك المبدأ وجوهره . وكذلك وصول الحق إلى صاحبه ليس حسناً إلا لأن الله فطر الإنسان على التعلق بحاجات فهو لا يستطيع الانفكاك عنها ، فكانت بذلك حقاً له .. ولو فطره على طراز آخر ولم يجعله محـتـاجـاً إليها ولا متعلقاً بشيء منها ، لما بحث عنها ، فما كانت بذلك حقاً له ، فما كان تفويتها عليه ظلماً ، ولا حفظها له عدلاً .
☆ 3 - Nothing is obligatory upon God, and good and evil in things are conventional. Perhaps you realize, if you reflect on this title, that it is a necessary consequence of the previous truth we have clarified. For if it is established that there is no intermediary between God and the creation of anything that His will has attached to its creation, and that all existents including their modalities and accidents are only by direct creation from God — then it is established that things do not inherently contain anything of good or evil, i.e., they cannot be characterized by a good or evil that is essential in them by nature, not by creation. For God's creation of all things with all their attributes requires that He is the Creator of the thing, and He is the Creator of the meaning of good and the meaning of evil, and then He is the connector and unifier between that thing and this meaning. And if you grasp this truth, you grasp alongside it that good or evil has no essential roots connected to the essence of the thing such that it cannot be separated from it, but rather it is a meaning that follows a ruling from the rulings of God Almighty, and that is what we call good or evil. And if God willed, He could reverse the matter and make good evil and evil good, as long as everything is by God's creation and His judgment. And this is the meaning of our statement: good and evil in things are conventional. And perhaps you wonder and say: How can I understand that the goodness of truthfulness and justice is conventional and not essential in them, or that the evil of lying and injustice is conventional and not essential in them?! The answer: that goodness or evil in such matters springs from several aspects, all of which are conventional and external to the essence of these matters and their substance. So the goodness of truthfulness is either derived from the fact that it leads to various benefits that accrue to the truthful person, or from the fact that he is rewarded for it on the Day of Resurrection, or from the fact that souls are naturally disposed to respect the truthful and feel aversion to the liar. And all of these, as you see, are motivations external to the essence of truthfulness itself. And this means that God was and still is able to transform souls and their dispositions so that they do not become attached to love of truthfulness nor feel aversion to lying. And similarly concerning principles of justice, for example: we only consider them good because they ensure that every rightful person receives his right, which is a cause, and that is external to the essence of that principle and its substance. Likewise, the delivery of a right to its owner is not good except because God has created man with attachment to needs, so he cannot separate himself from them, thus they become a right for him. And if He had created him according to another pattern and not made him in need of them nor attached to anything of them, he would not have sought them, so they would not be a right for him, so depriving him of them would not be injustice, nor preserving them for him justice.
Source pages p. 149

Commentary
This passage is a kalam proof that good and evil are not intrinsic (dhatī) but conventional (i'tibārī). The author begins by stating the title: 'Nothing is obligatory upon God, and good and evil in things are conventional.' He then explains that this follows logically from the previously established truth that there is no intermediary between God and creation — God is the direct creator of everything, including all attributes and accidents. If this is so, then things cannot inherently contain good or evil, because good and evil are also created by God. Instead, God creates the thing and then creates the meaning of good or evil and connects them. Therefore, the good or evil of an action is not a necessary property of that action but a judgment (hukm) from God, which could be reversed if He willed. The author anticipates an objection: how can we understand that truthfulness and justice are not inherently good? He answers by enumerating the external causes for why we consider them good: truthfulness leads to benefits, brings reward in the afterlife, and aligns with human natural disposition (fitra) to respect truth and abhor lies. All these reasons are external to the act itself. He further argues that God could change human nature to reverse these dispositions, proving that our moral valuations are contingent on God's creation. He extends the example to justice, showing that what we consider rights depend on God's having created humans with needs. If God had created humans differently, those same actions would not be considered good or just. Thus, the conclusion stands: good and evil are conventional, rooted in God's will and creation, not in the essence of things.

Key Terms
لا يجب على الله
الحسن والقبح
اعتباري
ذاتي
الخالق
الحكم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That good and evil are intrinsic properties of actions, independent of God's will.
Correction: Buti argues that if God creates everything directly, then no action has inherent moral value; moral qualities are created by God and could be reversed.

Checkpoint
According to Buti, why can things not inherently contain good or evil?
A) Because human reason can never know moral truths.
B) Because God directly creates all things and their attributes.
C) Because good and evil are purely social conventions.
D) Because the Prophet (peace be upon him) said so.

Key Takeaway
Good and evil are not intrinsic to actions but are conventional meanings created by God and attached to actions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If good and evil are conventional meanings created by God, what does that say about your moral judgments that you hold so firmly? Are you willing to submit them to God's command even if it reverses your natural inclinations?
?
Buti says God could make evil good and good evil. Does this idea unsettle you? Why? What does your reaction reveal about your attachment to your own sense of right and wrong?
?
You claim to believe that God is the direct creator of all things. But when you label an action as evil, do you unconsciously assume that evil is something inherent and beyond God's creation? How will you train yourself to see every moral valuation as a divine decree rather than an objective fact?

Divine Attributes
